I have no idea why, for so long, I thought the Sex God Robbie was a good choice for Georgia. Dave is a total dream boat...<br /><br />...and yes, I know I am twice his age.<br /><br />This snippet is for my present and future entertainment:<br /><br /><em>8:35 pm<br />You can make a sort of nose sling out of pair of knickers [panties:]!   <span style="display:none" id="freeText10268467340630090335">As seen on <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/05/on-the-bright-side-im-now-the-girlfriend-of-a-sex-god-by-louise-rennison.html">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />The only thing I am going to say here is that Dave the Laugh is the best boyfriend ever. I have no idea why, for so long, I thought the Sex God Robbie was a good choice for Georgia. Dave is a total dream boat...<br /><br />...and yes, I know I am twice his age.<br /><br />This snippet is for my present and future entertainment:<br /><br /><em>8:35 pm<br />You can make a sort of nose sling out of pair of knickers [panties:]! Like a sort of antigravity device. You put a leg hole over each ear and the middley bit supports your nose. It's quite comfy. I'm not saying that it looks very glamorous. I'm just saying it's comfy.<br /><br />8:40 pm<br />It's not something I would wear outside of the privacy of my own bedroom.<br /><br />8:45 pm<br />It's a good view from my windowsill. I can see Mr. Next Door with his stupid poodles. He's all happy now that Angus has gone off poodle baiting in favor of the Burmese sex kitten.<br /><br />8:46 pm<br />Oh hello, here comes Mark, my ex, the breast fondler. At this rate he will be the one and only fondler. I will die unfondled. He must be coming home from footie practice. I don't know how I could ever have thought about snogging him; he wears extremely tragic trousers. He is looking up at my window. He has seen me. He's stopped walking and is looking up at my window. Staring at me. Well, you know what they say - once a boy magnet always a boy magnet. I'm just going to stare back in a really cool way. All right, Mr. Big Gob, Mr. Dumper. I might be the dumpee but you still can't take your eyes away from me though, can you??? I still fascinate him. He's just looking up at me. Just staring and staring.<br />Mesmerized by me.<br /><br />8:50 pm<br />Oh my god! I am still wearing my nose hammock made out of knickers.<br /><br />8:56 pm<br />Mark will tell all his mates.<br /><br />8:57 pm<br />He will now call me a knicker-sniffer as well as a lesbian...</em><br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3070540-kristina-horner?shelf=childhood-books" class="actionLinkLite">childhood-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer81990368">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14528876429274069157"> I think I liked the second book even more than the first one in the series, because Dave the Laugh is my favorite character. I love Georgia's confusion as to whether it's more important to have a boyfriend who makes you go jelloid or one who makes you laugh.<br />Really enjoying this re-read of the series. Bring on the next one!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/202704997?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 02, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2461560-nicola" class="user" title="Nicola ">Nicola </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/864762.It_s_OK_I_m_Wearing_Really_Big_Knickers" title="Paperback 9780007218684" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2461560-nicola?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer202704997">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8271856673225957306">This book was every bit as fun as I expected it to be. This series is just really cute, funny and light-hearted. Georgia is simply hilarious and I never tire of her dramatic reactions. Her witty diary entries are infectious and I find them impossible to look away from. This installment did drag at parts but it was mostly as entertaining and amusing as the first. I'm certainly looking forward to see what else is in store for Georgia. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/15721970-sam?shelf=on-bookshelf" class="actionLinkLite">on-bookshelf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer980191873">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14284698912697719102"><strong>4 LAUGH AT LOUD STARS!</strong><br /><br /><em>“He said, 'Hi, gorgeous,' which I think is nice. I admire honesty.”</em><br /><br />So, once again Georgia Nicolson made laugh a lot with her occurences. I swear that I would ditch this book if it wasn't for all the stupid and funny things she said, because the story perse is boring.<br /><br /><em>“She got up and started making her hair have more bouncability with the air brush thing again. I waited until she had got it just right (in her opinion); then I hit her over the head with a pillow. She started t</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14284698912697719102"><strong>4 LAUGH AT LOUD STARS!</strong><br /><br /><em>“He said, 'Hi, gorgeous,' which I think is nice. I admire honesty.”</em><br /><br />So, once again Georgia Nicolson made laugh a lot with her occurences. I swear that I would ditch this book if it wasn't for all the stupid and funny things she said, because the story perse is boring.<br /><br /><em>“She got up and started making her hair have more bouncability with the air brush thing again. I waited until she had got it just right (in her opinion); then I hit her over the head with a pillow. She started to say, "Look, this is not funn-" but before she could finish I hit her over the head again with the pillow. And every time she tried to talk I did it again. She got all red-faced, which in Jas's case is very red indeed. It made me feel much better. Violence may be the answer to the world's problems. I may write to the Dalai Lama and suggest he tries my new approach.”</em><br /><br />She is a BULLY! Everything is against Jas, and poor her that I don't know how they still friends. Georgia gives the most horrible tips and advices. Jas has like broke up twice with her boyfriends thanks to Georgia. Thank God that Jas is not that dumb and she comes back to him, because they are a really sweet couple. Another sweet couple is Sven and Rosie. Sven made laugh every time he apperead, because no one ever understands what he is saying.<br /><br /><em>“Fortunately (or unfortunately, depending on where you were sitting) Libby let off the smelliest, loudest fart known to humanity. It came out of her bum-oley with such force that she lifted off my knee - like a hovercraft. Even she looked surprised by what had come out of her.”</em><br /><br />I'm trying to understand if Georgia's sister, Liberty aka Libbs, has a problem because she does the most random and weird things. I don't remember my sister or me doing those things. Plus her mother is always ignoring her like she doesn't care, i hate it.<br /><br /><em>“Boys are like elastic bands... Boys are different from girls. Girls like to be cozy all the time but boys don't. First of all, they like to get all close to you like a coiled-up rubber band, but after a while, they get fed up with being too coiled and need to stretch away to their full stretchiness. Then, after a bit of on-their-own strategy, they ping back to be close to you.”</em><br /><br />I'm trying to understand Georgia's way, I do, but I can't. Is she is so in love with Robbie, why is she so stupid in front of him. I guess that she turns more than jelly thanks to love? <em>Sacré Bleu!</em> Why I'm still reading this? I don't know. Will I keep reading it? <em>Sí</em>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13944907645292971576">What I like most about the Georgia Nicolson series is that it doesn’t try to be posh. It strives for absurdosity and succeeds. This installment picked up where <a title="Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/402013.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_">Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a> left off, with Georgia losing the SG and protesting a move to Kiwi-a-gogo Land (a.k.a. New Zealand). From there, it only gets crazier: cat mating, Elastic Band theory, Dr. George Clooney, the German language, a wheelbarrow, etc. <br /><br />Georgia is like the friend you want to dope slap, but just shake your h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13944907645292971576">What I like most about the Georgia Nicolson series is that it doesn’t try to be posh. It strives for absurdosity and succeeds. This installment picked up where <a title="Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson, #1) by Louise Rennison" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/402013.Angus__Thongs_and_Full_Frontal_Snogging__Confessions_of_Georgia_Nicolson___1_">Angus, Thongs and Full-Frontal Snogging</a> left off, with Georgia losing the SG and protesting a move to Kiwi-a-gogo Land (a.k.a. New Zealand). From there, it only gets crazier: cat mating, Elastic Band theory, Dr. George Clooney, the German language, a wheelbarrow, etc. <br /><br />Georgia is like the friend you want to dope slap, but just shake your head and laugh at instead because you realize whatever you do won’t make a lick of difference. She’s going to do mad things no matter what. That’s why glimpses of her nicer side are so surprising. Deep down beneath the stupidity and shallowness and mascara is a good person. Deep, deep down. <br /><br />Anyway, is it wrong that I dislike the SG and think Georgia should beg Dave the Laugh (a.k.a. best boyfriend EVER) to take her back? <em>Nein</em>? Thought so.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4276136023646736976">Oh, what’s the matter with that Georgia! How could she do that to the poor kid? Dave the Laugh’s the perfect guy… “Dave phoned. He said, ‘I just called to say I really liked you. Night night.’” I think that’s really cute. How could she not fall in love? Oh, I don’t know… but there’s definitely something off with that “Sex God” of hers. When I think about the two of them, that jailbait infatuation, it congers up an image of Gidget and the Kahuna. ;) But it’ll probably end the same way with Gidget</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4276136023646736976">Oh, what’s the matter with that Georgia! How could she do that to the poor kid? Dave the Laugh’s the perfect guy… “Dave phoned. He said, ‘I just called to say I really liked you. Night night.’” I think that’s really cute. How could she not fall in love? Oh, I don’t know… but there’s definitely something off with that “Sex God” of hers. When I think about the two of them, that jailbait infatuation, it congers up an image of Gidget and the Kahuna. ;) But it’ll probably end the same way with Gidget getting her Moondoggie. But it’ll be fun to see how it’ll all play out. <br /><br />But like in <em>Angus</em>, there are quite a few priceless gem moments:<br /><br />“I hope I am not being driven to the brink of madness by grief. They say that some people never get over things, like whatshername, Kathy Thing. The one who wandered over the moors at night yelling, ‘Heathcliffe, Heathcliffe, it’s me a-Kathy come home again.’”<br /><br />“I’ve spent so much time in bed I’ll probably start growing a long white beard soon, like Rip van Thing.”<br /><br />“I could be like a sad old sadsack or I could gird my loins and be like in that song. The one where you have to search for the hero within yourself. Jas was waiting for me at the bus stop. She said, ‘Why are you walking in that stiff way?’ ‘I’m girding my loins.’ ‘Well, it looks painful, like you’ve got a stick up your bottom.’”<br /></span>

  <a href="/user/show/6227263-silvia" class="left imgcol" title="Silvia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1327038620p2/6227263.jpg" alt="Silvia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/265714370?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 21, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6227263-silvia" class="user" title="Silvia">Silvia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7740127-on-the-bright-side-i-m-now-the-girlfriend-of-a-sex-god" title="Paperback 9780641925771" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer265714370">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12966986390670354748">I was in the library looking for a book to read, and I came across this one that I had actually failed at finding before. Georgia Nicolson comes back as funny as ever, she is now the girlfriend of Robbie (who she calls Sex God) and she thinks of nothing but snogging him. When he dumps her for being "too young" she tries to finds a way to get him back. There were many quotes that I love in the book, but one of my favourites was "What is there to laugh at? I am on the rack of love. Life is a sham</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12966986390670354748">I was in the library looking for a book to read, and I came across this one that I had actually failed at finding before. Georgia Nicolson comes back as funny as ever, she is now the girlfriend of Robbie (who she calls Sex God) and she thinks of nothing but snogging him. When he dumps her for being "too young" she tries to finds a way to get him back. There were many quotes that I love in the book, but one of my favourites was "What is there to laugh at? I am on the rack of love. Life is a sham and a facsimile and a farce." The quote shows Georgia's frustration with her life at the moment, but also shows a bit of her comical side. I loved how the author wrote in first-person, she did a great job writing down the thoughts of a 14 year old. It was fun reading the bits she wrote in French and in German also. I recommend this book to girls in need of a laugh, and who are experiencing boy problems. This book doesn't offer a good solution to those problems, but it sure lets you laugh non-stop about them. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12966986390670354748">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1147994413">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7027295146290862172"><strong>Actual rating:</strong> 1.5 stars<br /><br /><strong>Initial thoughts:</strong> My intention was to read all the books in the series. I don't think that's gonna happen after all. The first book was half-way entertaining. This second one was tiresome to read. There were some amusing moments but on the whole it wasn't all that funny. Georgia is beyond self-absorbed. Sure, it's her diary and she's 14 but she shows no respect for anyone in her life, not even her best friend. In fact, she displays no true affection for her best friend at</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7027295146290862172"><strong>Actual rating:</strong> 1.5 stars<br /><br /><strong>Initial thoughts:</strong> My intention was to read all the books in the series. I don't think that's gonna happen after all. The first book was half-way entertaining. This second one was tiresome to read. There were some amusing moments but on the whole it wasn't all that funny. Georgia is beyond self-absorbed. Sure, it's her diary and she's 14 but she shows no respect for anyone in her life, not even her best friend. In fact, she displays no true affection for her best friend at all. She's incredibly rude to people around her in the name of humour. I'm not buying it. The prose annoyed me too with all these made up words and repetitions. The only strength I found was the consistency of Georgia's character, which I didn't even like reading anymore.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17796167666410855419">I recognize that this series is completley ridiculous; that doesn't mean I don't really like it. I got this from the library yesterday. I also finished it yesterday. They're really fast reads. <br /><br />A few things: <br />- Whenever I read these books I feel the urge to talk like Georgia, good thing I don't. I"m sure I'd get REALLY strange looks. <br />- Reading this I realized Georgia is a kind of a shitty friend. She gets mad at Jas over the stupidest stuff, especially whenever she wants to talk about herself or Tom.<br />- I like Dave the Laugh a whole lot more than the Sex God. She's herself around him. When she's around Robbie she just acts weird, doesn't say much, and just makes out with him. They never talk about anything. All he does is kiss her. Sure, he's "The Sex God", but he doesn't have much of a personality, at least when he's around Georgia.<br /><br />I'm almost done with the third one now. I only got the second, third, and fourth one, so I'll probably go to the library again soon even though I have a bunch of my own books to read. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/840498697?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 07, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6679618-christina" class="user" title="Christina">Christina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/864762.It_s_OK_I_m_Wearing_Really_Big_Knickers" title="Paperback 9780007218684" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6679618-christina?shelf=romance-realistic" class="actionLinkLite">romance-realistic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6679618-christina?shelf=2014-snakes-n-ladders" class="actionLinkLite">2014-snakes-n-ladders</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer840498697">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13921828392412145774">It's OK, I'm Wearing Really Big Knickers was another barrel of laughs, but it just wasn't as good as the first book which was Marvy and double cool with knobs. The story continues from where we left off in the first book. Mutti (Mum) delivers the news that they are going to New Zealand to see Vati (Dad). And what perfect timing for Georgia - after finally becoming the girlfriend of a Sex God! <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[But not to worry, soon we find out that Vati had an accident with a rogue bore and is com</span></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13921828392412145774">It's OK, I'm Wearing Really Big Knickers was another barrel of laughs, but it just wasn't as good as the first book which was Marvy and double cool with knobs. The story continues from where we left off in the first book. Mutti (Mum) delivers the news that they are going to New Zealand to see Vati (Dad). And what perfect timing for Georgia - after finally becoming the girlfriend of a Sex God! <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[But not to worry, soon we find out that Vati had an accident with a rogue bore and is coming home! Perfectamondo! One problem solved.<br /><br />But another problems comes Georgia's way in the form of SG pulling out the 'I just realised again that you're too young for me' card and telling her that his mate Dave is a laugh. Georgia's mum's book <em>Men are from Mars</em> explains that boys are like elastic bands. Give boys space and they will stretch far away but eventually they will spring back. Hence, Georgia begins Operation Elastic Band, to get SG back with Dave the Laugh as the red herring. <br /><br />We continue to follow Georgia's amusing life at school, notably wearing berets like lunchpacks, getting sat on by the Bummer Twins, and playing hockey in three pairs of knickers. Meanwhile at home, Mum finds any excuse to go see Doctor George Clooney-lookalike, Angus finds a Burmese sex kitten from across the road and Libby continues developing her speech and making a poo mess everywhere.<br /><br />SG rarely makes an appearance, if only to shatter Georgia's heart, with Wet Lindsay entering his car. What's more, he doesn't even contact Georgia until the end (when she is suspended from school)! SG takes her to the park, tells her he can't forget her and commences a snogfest. Hurrah, they are to become official after her 15th birthday! <br /><br />And what? Georgia's family is going to Scotland for a week now? <br /><br />This book didn't leave us with such an ohmygod ending as the first. I really wish there was more of Robbie and Georgia. I feel as though Robbie hasn't gotten the chance to know Georgia properly. Obviously we know Georgia is a hilarious girl with a great personality but with Robbie she goes jelloid and can't even talk properly! I really hope the next books will develop their relationship better!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_41608788">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41608788" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1710557-bookczuk" class="left imgcol" title="bookczuk"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1228146591p2/1710557.jpg" alt="bookczuk" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/41608788?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1710557-bookczuk" class="user" title="bookczuk">bookczuk</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/402014.On_the_Bright_Side_I_m_Now_the_Girlfriend_of_a_Sex_God" title="Hardcover 9780060288136" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1710557-bookczuk?shelf=give-me-my-time-back" class="actionLinkLite">give-me-my-time-back</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1710557-bookczuk?shelf=ho-hum" class="actionLinkLite">ho-hum</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer41608788">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11644929317873303209">This was given to me by a friend. I actually read the first book by this author, which I thought was Bridget Jones but with teenage angst. The best character was Angus the wild cat. The humor was there but wore thin pretty quickly. The best thing about this was the title, IMO.<br /><br />Amazon Editorial Review:<br /><br />Fourteen-year-old Georgia Nicolson is back in British author Louise Rennison's irreverent, laugh-out-loud sequel to the Michael L. Printz Honor Book Angus, Thongs, and Full-Frontal Snogging. Written</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11644929317873303209">This was given to me by a friend. I actually read the first book by this author, which I thought was Bridget Jones but with teenage angst. The best character was Angus the wild cat. The humor was there but wore thin pretty quickly. The best thing about this was the title, IMO.<br /><br />Amazon Editorial Review:<br /><br />Fourteen-year-old Georgia Nicolson is back in British author Louise Rennison's irreverent, laugh-out-loud sequel to the Michael L. Printz Honor Book Angus, Thongs, and Full-Frontal Snogging. Written in diary form, these truly hilarious books chronicle the often minute-by-minute, very dramatic, and significant flip-flops of a teenager's psyche.<br /><br />7:18 p.m.<br />My eyes are all swollen up like mice eyes from crying. Even my nose is swollen. It's not small at the best of times, but now it looks like I've got three cheeks. Marvelous. Thank you, God.<br /><br />9:00 p.m.<br />I'll never get over this.<br /><br />9:10 p.m.<br />Time goes very slowly when you're suicidal.<br /><br />What tragedy has her so distraught? Her parents have told her she's moving to New Zealand just when she's managed to snog (kiss--look it up in the glossary) the SG (Sex God, a.k.a Robbie). This is of course not the only source of drama in Georgia's eventful life. Her half Scottish wildcat, Angus, who is the size of a small Labrador, herds the poodles next door and terrorizes the neighborhood. Her little sister, Libby, who is slightly mad, stores her "pooey knickers" and her scuba-diving Barbie doll in Georgia's bed. Her mother (from whom she inherited her orangutan eyebrow gene and possibly her "gigantic basoomas") is clearly inhabiting Earth solely to make her life miserable, and even her best friend Jas is "half girl, half turnip."<br /><br />Despite the fact that she's spared from going to "Kiwi-a-gogo land," things don't get much better for Georgia. She's suspended for a childish prank right before her dad returns from New Zealand, she falls in love with the SG who dumps her for being too young, and Dave, the "red-herring" boyfriend she's using to make the SG jealous calls her a "heartless whatsit." And, she continues, "the spot on my bum is probably a boil. I wonder what Buddha would do now?" Rennison's comedic timing is brilliant. Adolescent angst ("I hope I am not driven to the brink of madness by grief") vanishes less than an hour later ("Angus can fetch sticks!!!") and sometimes even sooner. (Warning: Do not read this book while riding a train or bus unless you don't care what people think of intermittent explosive laughter. Seriously.) (Ages 12 and older) --Karin Snelson</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11644929317873303209">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40917054" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1169804-steph-reviewer-x" class="left imgcol" title="Steph (Reviewer X)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1211073600p2/1169804.jpg" alt="Steph (Reviewer X)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/40917054?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 02, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1169804-steph-reviewer-x" class="user" title="Steph (Reviewer X)">Steph (Reviewer X)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/402014.On_the_Bright_Side_I_m_Now_the_Girlfriend_of_a_Sex_God" title="Hardcover 9780060288136" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer40917054">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8594747297931257262">Cross-posted from my <strong> <a rel="nofollow" href="http://reviewerx.blogspot.com/2009/05/why-georgia-nicolson-rocks.html">blog post.</a> </strong><br /><br /><strong>Why Georgia Nicolson Rocks<br />(On the Bright Side, I'm Now The Girlfriend of a Sex God edition)</strong><br /><br />1. She calls breasts “basoomas” and, less commonly, “nunga nungas”. (“‘Well, he says that if you get hold of a breast and pull it out and then let it go…it goes nunga nunga nunga!’”)<br /><br />2. She seems obsessed with pants/shorts. Besides the obvious metaphorical “nuddy-pants” and “furry-shorts” (which we see in later titles), she’s always going on about how big someone’s shorts ar</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8594747297931257262">Cross-posted from my <strong>
  <a rel="nofollow" href="http://reviewerx.blogspot.com/2009/05/why-georgia-nicolson-rocks.html">blog post.</a>
</strong><br /><br /><strong>Why Georgia Nicolson Rocks<br />(On the Bright Side, I'm Now The Girlfriend of a Sex God edition)</strong><br /><br />1. She calls breasts “basoomas” and, less commonly, “nunga nungas”. (“‘Well, he says that if you get hold of a breast and pull it out and then let it go…it goes nunga nunga nunga!’”)<br /><br />2. She seems obsessed with pants/shorts. Besides the obvious metaphorical “nuddy-pants” and “furry-shorts” (which we see in later titles), she’s always going on about how big someone’s shorts are and how frightening that is. More commonly her granddad’s.<br /><br />3. She’s British, so she uses Britishisms, like tosser, bloke, marvy, fringe, loo, and knickers. And many more.<br /><br />4. She becomes a “Buddhist” after God fails to give her the Sex God back.<br /><br />5. It’s hard to tell which of Georgia’s friends are more self-obsessed reading these, but it’s fun to read anyhow because it’s not smutty self-obsession a la Gossip Girl, but rather a comical variety. (Jas: I’m dying. Georgia: Shut up, now, Jas. [minutes later:] G: I wonder if the Sex God will call me. J: Tom called me last night.)<br /><br />6, She does the pencil test. You know, putting it under your nunga nunga and if it stays there, you need to wear a bra? Ah, to be at that stage when wearing a bra seems like the worst thing in the world…<br /><br />7. (And she’s 14! Ha! I and most of my friends went through that when we were 10/11!)<br /><br />8. She’s got a cat the size-of-a-small-Labrador, the half-Scottish-wildcat Angus, who courts the Burmese pedigree “minx” across the street by strutting his stuff.<br /><br />9. She never quite knows what she’s on about, and says so on multiple occasions.<br /><br />10. And there’s nowhere else you can get a collection of quotes quite like these:<br /><br />#1: Ellen told me that her brother and his friends go out on “cat patrol”.<br /><br />I said, do they really like cats, then?”<br /><br />She said, “No, him and his mates are the cat patrol and they go out looking for birds…you know, chicks…girls.”<br /><br />Good Lord.<br /><br />#2: “We’ve just rang to say we’ve made up this great new dance; it’s called ‘The phone box.’”<br /><br />She played a radio down the phone and in the background I could hear a lot of grunting and shuffling and Sven going, “Oh jah oh jah, hit it, lads!” or something in Swedish or whatever it is he speaks. Gibberish,. Normally. Not English, anyway. Then there was a bit of what sounded like tap-dancing. Rosie came back on the phone all breathless. “Brilliant, eh? See you in the next world…don’t be late!!” And she slammed the phone down.<br /><br />#3: “Miss Simpson, it is a well-known fact that if friends sit together they are encouraged to do more work.” But she just shook in such a jelloid way I thought her chins would drop off.<br /><br />She said, “The last time you two sat together, you set locusts free in the biology lab.”<br /><br />Oh honestly; not only has she got legs like an elephant, she’s got a memory like one.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8594747297931257262">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer439498485">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16538077826164075561">This book is kind of set up like a diary yet some pages tell the story as it is happening. Georgia is a girl who is growing up. She is 14 and her family may be making a huge move. She is so upset about this because she is the girlfriend of a Sex God. She writes about all her feelings and sometimes it is very random or she will rant about the same problem for a while. The Sex God is an older boy who keeps their relationship a secret at first. They meet a few times and kiss or as they call it, sno</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16538077826164075561">This book is kind of set up like a diary yet some pages tell the story as it is happening. Georgia is a girl who is growing up. She is 14 and her family may be making a huge move. She is so upset about this because she is the girlfriend of a Sex God. She writes about all her feelings and sometimes it is very random or she will rant about the same problem for a while. The Sex God is an older boy who keeps their relationship a secret at first. They meet a few times and kiss or as they call it, snogging. Did I mention it is a British novel and is of course written with British words. he Sex God decides that Georgia is too young for him who is 18 and may be going away for school. Will he ever realize that love is a powerful thing? Will Georgia end up moving away from all her problems?<br /><br />I thought this was pretty funny. I liked how the author put a dictionary in the back explaining the different British terms. Georgia is pretty funny and most defiantly a teenager who is in the prime of growing up. She has fun with life. It does seem like she is a very pretty girl and gets by on her looks a lot. I believe the younger side of young adults would enjoy this sort of a love story that many may be able to relate too and it is cool it is British.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1473994322670553644">Hah!This book was HILARIOUS!!!! I think that some of the characters are just absolutely crazy.Georgia is quite a character. She is funny and witty sometimes, but to be completely honest it doesn't seem like she's a very nice person. I mean, she bosses around her friends and says really hurtful things about them.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText1473994322670553644">Hah!This book was HILARIOUS!!!! I think that some of the characters are just absolutely crazy.Georgia is quite a character. She is funny and witty sometimes, but to be completely honest it doesn't seem like she's a very nice person. I mean, she bosses around her friends and says really hurtful things about them. Like with Jas. That girl is Georgia's target and she's one of her best friends! I really don't get why any of Georgia friends would want to stay buddies with her.<br /><br />Have you ever had one of those friendships, where there is a more dominant friend? Well, it's really not fun! i guess you could say that its like getting bullied but with someone closer. I mean, are these people really friends if they are mean to you and make fun of you? I'm not saying that i don't like the book, i just don't LOVE the main character.But, Georgia can be kinda funny. Okay maybe A LOT funny!<br /><br />I have to say, Georgia has a pretty good sense of humor. Although she can be rude and disrespectful, she comes up with interseting things.She also kind of pushes the buttons of the adults in her life but that's just who she is. But something kind of confuses me. In the book Georgia said that she like being with Dave, so why did she brake up with him and tell him that she was just using him? She could have been really happy with him and then she just kind of ruined it.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_62691017">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62691017" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/398239-michelle" class="left imgcol" title="Michelle"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448427826p2/398239.jpg" alt="Michelle" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/62691017?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 08, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/398239-michelle" class="user" title="Michelle">Michelle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/402014.On_the_Bright_Side_I_m_Now_the_Girlfriend_of_a_Sex_God" title="Hardcover 9780060288136" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">the georgia crew</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=pure-comedy" class="actionLinkLite">pure-comedy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/398239-michelle?shelf=2009" class="actionLinkLite">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62691017">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1580113873245974046">I hereby admit that I am a fan-girl of Georgia Nicolson.<br /><br />Once again, Georgia did not disappoint. This second book in Louise Rennison's all too funny series about young Georgia Nicolson - British teenager extraordinaire - was perfect. It picks up just after she has discovered that Vati (her father) will be moving her family to Kiwi-a-gogo Land (New Zealand) and thus her life is effectually over. After snagging (and snogging) the Sex God (aka Robbie) in the previous book, Georgia is still up to her</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1580113873245974046">I hereby admit that I am a fan-girl of Georgia Nicolson.<br /><br />Once again, Georgia did not disappoint. This second book in Louise Rennison's all too funny series about young Georgia Nicolson - British teenager extraordinaire - was perfect. It picks up just after she has discovered that Vati (her father) will be moving her family to Kiwi-a-gogo Land (New Zealand) and thus her life is effectually over. After snagging (and snogging) the Sex God (aka Robbie) in the previous book, Georgia is still up to her old tricks - figuring out new ways to annoy her teachers, avoiding Wet Lindsay, and trying to figure out exactly what a boy means by "I'll see you later."? I really don't know how she gets into the messes she does but I can't help but enjoy every minute of her crazy life.<br /><br />Georgia's life is detailed in irreverent diary entries where she honestly lays down the good, the bad, and the ugly of teendom without ever becoming preachy or campy. She is completely self-centered but still entirely lovable in the way only teenagers can be. I love the scrapes she gets into and I love, love how she tries to explain new concepts to her friends. I about split my shorts laughing when she tried to explain to the Ace gang how Dave the Laugh will become her Red Herring. Fabbity fab fab.<br /><br />All I can say is Louise Rennison should be very careful to not be drinking anything while she comes up with some of the stuff Georgia gets herself into. I know from sad experience it shouldn't be attempted.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1580113873245974046">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer137140132">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11405810905127896465">On the Bright Side, I'm Now the Girlfriend of a Sex God: Further Confessions of Georgia Nicolson by Louise Rennison talks about a group of losers (girls) that saw two new gods in their school on the first day. One of those girls was Georgia Nicolson that fell in love with a 17-year-old prince charming named Robbie. Georgia tried several times to impress him, but the more she tried the more things were worse. Robbie loved it when Georgia messed up. After a while, Robbie started dating a popular,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11405810905127896465">On the Bright Side, I'm Now the Girlfriend of a Sex God: Further Confessions of Georgia Nicolson by Louise Rennison talks about a group of losers (girls) that saw two new gods in their school on the first day. One of those girls was Georgia Nicolson that fell in love with a 17-year-old prince charming named Robbie. Georgia tried several times to impress him, but the more she tried the more things were worse. Robbie loved it when Georgia messed up. After a while, Robbie started dating a popular, mean and bossy girl. Georgia tried to find embarrassing things about the girl he was dating. After Georgia gave up, she decided to go with her family to New Zea-land where her father works. On her birthday, she went out with her mom to a night club to celebrate it. Georgia was surprised by all her friends and family there ready to celebrate her birthday. Moreover, Robbie chose to date Georgia instead of dating the fake girl. I highly recommend this book to mature-enough teenagers. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3374445843693362701">Rebecca Weimert<br />Humor<br /><br />Georgia Nicholson is 14 and crazy about the “Sex God” also known as her boyfriend Robbie. But when Robbie breaks up with her because he thinks he is too young she devises a plan to get him back. Georgia and her friends devise the Red Herring plan that involves a boy names Dave who she uses to get Robbie back. When she realizes she is falling for Dave she tells him the truth and breaks it off. This story follows Georgia’s hilarious intimate thoughts about her family, friends,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3374445843693362701">Rebecca Weimert<br />Humor<br /><br />Georgia Nicholson is 14 and crazy about the “Sex God” also known as her boyfriend Robbie. But when Robbie breaks up with her because he thinks he is too young she devises a plan to get him back. Georgia and her friends devise the Red Herring plan that involves a boy names Dave who she uses to get Robbie back. When she realizes she is falling for Dave she tells him the truth and breaks it off. This story follows Georgia’s hilarious intimate thoughts about her family, friends, and the Sex God.<br />Although this book had some funny parts, it was extremely difficult to understand. Georgia has her own language and unless you either have read the previous books or you read the dictionary of Georgia’s words first the reader would become lost and the story is difficult to follow. Because the story follows her thoughts it is easy to understand Georgia and the reader gets in insight to what she is really feeling.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14514944984051399947">Louise Rennison never disappoints! I was having the most awful week/weekend, and I picked up this second book of the series. I know, I know...the title seems sketch. I promise it's clean! Anyway, I have to read these books alone because I die laughing. Seriously. I chortle. No, it's more than that. I throw my head back, guffawing. I don't even know if "guffaw" is ever written with -ing, and if it's not, it's created now because that's exactly what happens when reading this series. So funny! I ju</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14514944984051399947">Louise Rennison never disappoints! I was having the most awful week/weekend, and I picked up this second book of the series. I know, I know...the title seems sketch. I promise it's clean! Anyway, I have to read these books alone because I die laughing. Seriously. I chortle. No, it's more than that. I throw my head back, guffawing. I don't even know if "guffaw" is ever written with -ing, and if it's not, it's created now because that's exactly what happens when reading this series. So funny! I just think it's doubly funny because she reminds me of myself at her age - just figuring out life, making stupid mistakes...hmm..sounds kind of like my current situation actually. Anyway, if you want a quick side-splitting read that you can't put down, read this series. I adore it. Excuse me now while I go read the third...</span>

      <a href="/user/show/2254007-grace" class="user" title="Grace">Grace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/402014.On_the_Bright_Side_I_m_Now_the_Girlfriend_of_a_Sex_God" title="Hardcover 9780060288136" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2254007-grace?shelf=only-once" class="actionLinkLite">only-once</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2254007-grace?shelf=for-fun" class="actionLinkLite">for-fun</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer76220756">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14793405475282024086">This is the story of a 14 year old British girl named Georgia. She is a traditional teenager with anxieties about boys, a silly way of looking a life, and nothing ever seems to go her way. <br /><br />The book is written sort of like a diary, but with time tags on it that made me think of Twitter. The only difference was between Rennison's writing style for this series of books and Twitter is the concept of no word limit in the diary entries. <br /><br />The content was young adultish, fun, and relaxing. For non-Brits,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14793405475282024086">This is the story of a 14 year old British girl named Georgia. She is a traditional teenager with anxieties about boys, a silly way of looking a life, and nothing ever seems to go her way. <br /><br />The book is written sort of like a diary, but with time tags on it that made me think of Twitter. The only difference was between Rennison's writing style for this series of books and Twitter is the concept of no word limit in the diary entries. <br /><br />The content was young adultish, fun, and relaxing. For non-Brits, Rennison adds a glossary of slang words in the back. Even that is written as if Georgia has written it and is talking directly to the reader. <br /><br />All in all, it was a fun and relaxing read. It didn't wow me, but I'll likely tell anyone that is looking for a light-hearted read to pick it up. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14793405475282024086">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Odp9HDOe+A6tzONWTNtA/PEPIJAMbQqe9jil205v+jFcDkLPwUzs9CEUl+0yuqZOuPjjiUWwTTScMaBJgvoMdA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

While living Britain, Emily\'s been given the chance&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText10332890136701319769\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;The Barnes &amp;amp; Noble Review\nThe teen with can-do attitude (and a little klutzy streak) who starred in The Year My Life Went Down the Loo is seeing Scots in this hilarious page-turner by Katie Maxwell.\n\nWhile living Britain, Emily\'s been given the chance to temporarily work on a sheep farm in Scotland\'s Highlands. Despite having scenery that\'s basically &amp;quot;mud, mud, a couple of dogs, and, surprise of all surprises, more mud,&amp;quot; the teen at least gets to feast her eyes on a dreamy shepherd named Ruaraidh. Of course, Emily -- and her cousin Holly -- are both gaga over the &amp;quot;Scottish love god&amp;quot; (never mind that he has six fingers on one hand), and after they decide to compete over who gets to snog him, the two get into more than a few capers involving a man-trap in an ancient castle, spray-painted sheep, and self-tanning lotion. Sound crazy? No doubt about that, but thank your lucky plaid kilt, Emily never fails to keep herself in high spirits, her fingers typing away to her Seattle BFF, and her Hottie of the Week list updated.\n\nFollowing in the footsteps of popular authors like Meg Cabot and Louise Rennison (Confessions of Georgia Nicolson), Maxwell delivers a character that speaks her mind while making you laugh out loud. Girls will appreciate her competitive boy-snogging gusto, and they\'ll be cheering for more tales about Emily when all is finished. Whether you already know what true Scotsmen wear under their kilts, Maxwell\'s novel is a real trip.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/65189.Louise_Rennison">About Louise Rennison</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/65189.Louise_Rennison"><img alt="65189" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1217261779p2/65189.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer7594478540775543945">Louise Rennison is the bestselling award-winning author of the phenomenally successful ‘Confessions of Georgia Nicolson’ series, translated into over 34 languages and to the stage and big screen as ‘Angus, Thongs and Perfect Snogging’. She has won the Nestle Smarties Book Prize, the Michael L. Printz Honor Book and the Roald Dahl Funny prize for ‘Withering Tights’.<br /></span>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/65189.Louise_Rennison" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Louise Rennison...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_5170850').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script>
</li>
</ul>
</div>
